# Incident Root-Cause: Grafana Dashboard Migration Field Config Loss

## Your Task

A Grafana dashboard migration (v38) silently drops table panel field override configuration during import. Dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` lose column widths and text alignment. Trace this bug to its root cause in the Grafana codebase. Find: 1. The Go source files under `pkg/services/dashboardimport/` or `pkg/services/dashboards/` that implement the v38 schema migration. 2. The specific function that handles `fieldConfig` merging and the conditional logic that fails for missing `defaults.custom`. 3. The schema version constant file that registers v38. Report the repo, file path, function name, and the flawed conditional expression for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor
... (truncated)

   135→// migrateOverrides updates the overrides configuration to use the new cellOptions format
   136→func migrateOverrides(fieldConfig map[string]interface{}) {
   137→	overrides, ok := fieldConfig["overrides"].([]interface{})
   138→	if !ok {
   139→		return
   140→	}
   141→
   142→	for _, override := range overrides {
   143→		o, ok := override.(map[string]interface{})
   144→		if !ok {
   145→			continue
   146→		}
   147→
   148→		properties, ok := o["properties"].([]interface{})
   149→		if !ok {
   150→			continue
   151→		}
   152→
   153→		for _, property := range properties {
   154→			prop, ok := property.(map[string]interface{})
   155→			if !ok {
   156→				continue
   157→			}
   158→
   159→			// Update the id to cellOptions
   160→			if prop["id"] == "custom.displayMode" {
   161→				prop["id"] = "custom.cellOptions"
   162→				if value, ok := prop["value"]; ok {
   163→					if valueStr, ok := value.(string); ok {
   164→						prop["value"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(valueStr)
   165→					}
   166→				} else {
   167→					// If no value exists, add empty cellOptions object to match frontend behavior
   168→					// Frontend always assigns a value even when original displayMode had no value
   169→					// See: public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts:880
   170→					// override.properties[j].value = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(overrideDisplayMode);
   171→					prop["value"] = map[string]interface{}{}
   172→				}
   173→			}
   174→		}
   175→	}
   176→}

     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor

// migrateOverrides updates the overrides configuration to use the new cellOptions format
func migrateOverrides(fieldConfig map[string]interface{}) {
	overrides, ok := fieldConfig["overrides"].([]interface{})
	if !ok {
		return

177-usertool_resultAgent
**FOUND THE BUG!!!** Look at line 608:

```go
if panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"] == true {
```

This condition is WRONG! Here's the problem:

The code is trying to preserve fieldConfig if the panel originally had custom. But the condition checks `== true`, which means:
- If `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` is true: preserve fieldConfig (lines 610-615)
- If `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` is false OR not set: delete fieldConfig (line 617)

But this is wrong! If a panel DIDN'T originally have custom BUT custom was ADDED during migration (like in V38 when processing overrides), then the flag will be false, and we'll delete fieldConfig and lose the custom properties!

**The bug is that line 608 should use `!=` instead of `==`!**

It should be:

```go
if panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"] != true {
```

OR, to handle the case where the flag doesn't exist:

```go
if !, hasFlag := panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"].(bool); !hasFlag || !hasFlag {
```

But wait, that still doesn't make sense. Let me think about what the CORRECT logic should be:

The code should preserve fieldConfig if:
1. The panel originally had custom, OR
2. The panel currently has custom (added during migration)

So the condition should check if custom exists NOW, not whether it existed in the original input!

The correct condition would be something like:

```go
if fieldConfig, ok := panelValue.(map[string]interface{}); ok {
    if defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {
        if _, hasCustom := defaults["custom"]; hasCustom || panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"] == true {
            // Preserve fieldConfig
            continue
        }
    }
}
delete(panel, prop)
```

Or more simply:

```go
if panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"] != true {

## Summary

I've successfully traced the Grafana v38 dashboard migration bug to its root cause and created a detailed analysis in `/workspace/answer.json`. Here are the key findings:

### **Root Cause: Flawed Conditional in Cleanup Phase**

**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`  
**Function:** `filterDefaultValues`  
**Line:** 608  
**Flawed Conditional:** `if panel["_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom"] == true {`

### **The Bug**

The condition only preserves `fieldConfig` if the panel **originally had** `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the input. However, when v38 migration adds `custom` properties (like `custom.cellOptions`) to field overrides, the flag is never set for dashboards that didn't originally have `defaults.custom`. This causes the cleanup phase to delete the entire `fieldConfig`, losing all custom field properties including column widths and text alignment.

### **Failure Scenario**
1. Dashboard input has `fieldConfig.defaults: {}` (empty) with field overrides containing `custom.displayMode`
2. V38 migration converts `custom.displayMode` → `custom.cellOptions` in overrides
3. Cleanup phase checks `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag (not set, since original had no custom)
4. Conditional fails, fieldConfig is deleted
5. Result: Column widths and alignment stored in custom field properties are lost

### **Implementation Chain**
- `migrations.go:GetMigrations()` → Registers V38
- `v38.go:V38()` → Initiates migration
- `v38.go:processPanelsV38()` → Processes table panels
- `v38.go:migrateOverrides()` → Converts displayMode to cellOptions (adds custom properties)
- `frontend_defaults.go:filterDefaultValues()` → **Incorrectly deletes fieldConfig due to flawed conditional at line 608**

The conditional should check if custom exists in the

The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it\n// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.\n//\n// The migration works by:\n// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)\n// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties\n// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode\n// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path\n// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features\n//\n// This restructuring provides several key benefits:\n// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)\n// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations\n// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode\n// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality\n//\n// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,\n// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.\n//\n// Example transformations:\n//\n// Before migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t isEqual(a, b interface{}) bool {\n   666\u2192\tif a == nil && b == nil {\n   667\u2192\t\treturn true\n   668\u2192\t}\n   669\u2192\tif a == nil || b == nil {\n   670\u2192\t\treturn false\n 700\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   701\u2192\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n   702\u2192\t\t\t\treturn false\n   703\u2192\t\t\t}\n   704\u2192\t\t\tfor k, v := range The root cause is a flawed conditional in the cleanup phase that fails to preserve fieldConfig when custom properties are added during migration but weren't present in the original input.\\n\\n### Root Cause Location\\n**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`  \\n**Function:** `filterDefaultValues`  \\n**Line:** 608  \\n**Flawed Conditional Expression:** `if panel[\\\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\\\"] == true {`\\n\\n### The Bug\\nThe condition on line 608 only preserves `fieldConfig` if the panel **originally had** `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in the input JSON. However, dashboards can gain `custom` properties during schema migrations (specifically during v38 when processing field overrides with `custom.displayMode`). When a dashboard never originally had `defaults.custom`, the `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag is not set, causing the conditional to fail and the entire `fieldConfig` to be deleted at line 620.\\n\\n### Failure Scenario\\n1. **Input Dashboard:** Has `fieldConfig.defaults: {}` (empty, no custom) with `fieldConfig.overrides` containing `custom.displayMode` properties\\n2. **v38 Migration:** `processPanelsV38()` converts `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` in the overrides\\n3. **Cleanup Phase:** `filterDefaultValues()` checks `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom` flag\\n4. **Condition Fails:** Flag is not set (original input had no custom), so condition at line 608 evaluates to false\\n5. **Data Loss:** `fieldConfig` is deleted at line 620, losing all `custom.cellOptions` properties added by v38\\n6. **Result:** Dashboard loses column widths, text alignment, and other custom field configurations stored in overrides\\n\\n### What the Conditional Should Check\\nThe condition should preserve `fieldConfig` if **either**:\\n1. The panel originally had `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` (current check: `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom == true`), **OR**\\n2. The panel currently has `defaults.custom` (added during migration) - **THIS CHECK IS MISSING**\\n\\nThe corrected logic should check if `custom` exists in the current fieldConfig structure, not just whether it existed in the original input.\\n\\n### Implementation Chain\\n1. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go (line 74):** Registers V38 migration\\n2. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go (V38 function):** Initiates migration via `processPanelsV38()`\\n3. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go (processPanelsV38):** Processes table panels and calls `migrateOverrides()`\\n4. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go (migrateOverrides):** Converts `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions` in field overrides (adds custom properties)\\n5. **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go (filterDefaultValues):** Cleanup phase that incorrectly removes fieldConfig due to the flawed conditional at line 608\\n\\n### The Flawed Conditional in Context\\n```go\\n// Line 606-620 in filterDefaultValues\\nif prop == \\\"fieldConfig\\\" {\\n    // Check if we need to preserve the custom object before removing fieldConfig\\n    if panel[\\\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\\\"] == true {  // <-- FLAWED LINE 608\\n        // Ensure fieldConfig structure exists with custom object\\n        if fieldConfig, ok := panelValue.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n            if defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\\\"defaults\\\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\\n                if _, hasCustom := defaults[\\\"custom\\\"]; !hasCustom {\\n                    defaults[\\\"custom\\\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\\n                }\\n                // Don't remove fieldConfig if we added custom back\\n                continue\\n            }\\n        }\\n    }\\n    delete(panel, prop)  // <-- Deletes fieldConfig when flag not set\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe condition should be inverted or expanded to also check if `defaults[\\\"custom\\\"]` exists **in the current fieldConfig**, not just whether it existed in the original input. A corrected version would check: `if panel[\\\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\\\"] == true || (current fieldConfig has custom)` before deciding to delete the fieldConfig.\\n\\n### Files and Functions Involved\\n- **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go:** `GetMigrations()` - Registers all schema migrations including V38\\n- **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:** `V38()`, `processPanelsV38()`, `migrateOverrides()` - Implements the displayMode to cellOptions conversion\\n- **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:** `filterDefaultValues()` - Contains the flawed conditional at line 608 that causes field config loss\\n\"\n}\n",
